Silk Industry Association

Held General Membership Meeting Yesterday

Promote Acceptance of Bills of Exchange and Other Matters

Elected Luo Qinghua and Others as Executive and Supervisory Committee Members

The Shanghai Silk Industry Association held its seventh general membership meeting at the City Chamber of Commerce at 3 PM yesterday. Wang Yucheng from the City Party Headquarters, Fan Aiwei from the Social Affairs Bureau, Yuan Hongjun from the City Chamber of Commerce, and more than 250 members attended. Luo Qinghua was publicly elected as chairman. The meeting amended the articles of association and re-elected executive and supervisory committee members. The details are as follows:

Chairman's Report

After the ceremony, Chairman Luo Qinghua gave a brief report, saying that the association is holding its seventh general membership meeting today. According to the association's articles of association, a general membership meeting should be held once every year in mid-June. This year's meeting was postponed to today due to the National Assembly election. Since the establishment of the association, it has been more than six years, during which time the country has been in a difficult period, which has greatly affected the silk industry market. The economic situation of the industry has encountered unprecedented difficulties. In the spring of last year, the association created the commercial acceptance bill of exchange system in order to activate the use of funds. For several months of promotion, it has been deeply supported by the domestic economic community. After the government reformed the currency system on November 4th last year, the matter has been resolved. However, since the rampant smuggling in North China, a large number of smuggled rayon has been imported, which is a fatal blow to the silk industry. It not only affects national taxation, but also poses a serious threat to the industry. Now that the national crisis is becoming more serious, it is hoped that the industry will concentrate its efforts to eliminate internal strife and strictly inspect smuggling, so that the association will become brighter and more prosperous. Representatives from party and government agencies then made speeches, followed by amendments to the articles of association, discussion of proposals, and re-election of executive and supervisory committee members. The meeting adjourned at around 6 PM.

Resolutions

(1) Zhang Xueliang's rebellion with troops, hijacking of the leader, and shaking of the national foundation should be condemned in the name of the general membership meeting. A telegram should be sent to urge Zhang Xueliang to repent and escort Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to a safe area. The resolution was passed. (2) According to the amount of money collected from the business leaders of each village, aid should be given to the soldiers fighting against the enemy in Suiyuan. The resolution was passed. (3) The resolution to amend the articles of association was passed. (4) Urge the industry to unanimously promote the municipal ruler. The principle was passed, and it was submitted to the next executive committee for handling. (5) Urge the industry to unanimously promote acceptance bills of exchange. The principle was passed, and it was submitted to the next executive committee for handling.

Elected Executive and Supervisory Committee Members

As a result of the election, there were 15 executive committee members: Luo Qinghua, Shen Qingsi, Pan Yisheng, Wu Xingcha, Suo Zuosun, Xu Limin, Li Yunjia, Li Wenzhi, Lou Fengshao, Wu Baoyuan, Shen Zicha, Yan Juqing, Niu Zhizhi, Pan Digong, Cheng Yansheng, etc. There were 7 supervisory committee members: Lu Zhengbing, Shen Qinzhai, Wang Tingsong, Niu Jiechen, Wang Shoushen, Cheng Yongliu, Wang Meisheng, etc.

Tax Bureau Explains

Tax Collection for Branch Stores

In response to an inquiry, the Income Tax Office of the Ministry of Finance replied to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday that the letter No. 1497 from your esteemed chamber stated that the Huoyou Industry Association stated in its letter of this month that Article 6 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations stipulates that the head office and its branch stores in the Republic of China, whose capital is divided from each other, should calculate their income separately. The meaning of the text naturally refers to the division of capital. From a systemic perspective, the branches belong to the head office or the head company, which is undoubtedly true. However, once the capital is divided, the operating rights are somewhat independent. It is also reasonable to levy taxes separately in the location of the branch store. However, many branch stores often do not divide the capital and only sell goods on behalf of the head office. In other words, whether there is profit or loss, the branch does not care. If the above situation occurs, should the same regulations still be applied to levy taxes in their location, or should the head office or the head company pay in total as a whole? Since the detailed rules of the regulations do not have clear provisions, the association is not very clear. Furthermore, although the branch store and the head office have a consistent organization, the brands are the same and different. It is not known whether there is any conflict. I would dare to inquire about two points, and I hope that your chamber will give an explanation, so that the association can forward it. Upon arrival, it was found that the branch store mentioned by the association only sells goods on behalf of the head office. In fact, the operating rights are not divided. The income tax should naturally be paid by the head office in total. This is a natural interpretation in accordance with the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations. However, for those whose name is a branch store, but the brand name is different from the head office, how should it be handled to avoid abuses? The Ministry of Finance is hereby requested to investigate and show a reply so that it can be forwarded, etc. As such, Article 6 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations stipulates that the capital of the head office and its branch stores, which are divided from each other, refers to the capital and business of the branch store being completely independent. If the brand name of the branch store is different from the head office, and its capital and business are not completely independent, its income will still be calculated together with the head office. The previous letter is hereby approved. The recipient is requested to check and inform.

The Yangtze River Rises Sharply

Shipping Routes Fully Open; Cargo Ships Operate Smoothly

The Thunderstorm's Merit Brings Joy to Shipping Merchants

Rose to Fifteen Feet Seven Inches Yesterday

The Yangtze River water receded, the earliest this year, and the retreat was also the most severe, once dropping to nine feet and three inches. The water level in Hankou dropped to two feet and four inches. Shanghai-Hankou ships could not go up the river after reaching Jiujiang, so Shanghai export ships could only load 20-30% of their cargo under the water level restrictions. At the same time, the boats and warehouses in Jiujiang were full of goods. The Yangtze River boatmen and shipping merchants were worried that the water level would recede further after the weather turned cold, and the shipping route would be cut off, and the accumulated goods waiting to be transported would not be able to be cleared. Unexpectedly, the weather changed unexpectedly. After the thunderstorm the day before yesterday, the Yangtze River water level changed dramatically, rising sharply. Yesterday, it was 13 feet and 7 inches, rising more than 4 feet in two days. This is the water level for the shallow sections from Jiujiang to Hankou. From Jiujiang to Wuhu, it has risen to 15 feet and 7 inches. The Yangtze River shipping route is fully open, and large cargo ships can be fully loaded with cargo and go directly to Hankou. Yesterday, the shipping merchants and the Yangtze River boatmen were overjoyed upon receiving this telegram. All the commercial goods that were accumulated in Shanghai, Wuhu, and Hankou due to the shallow water are now being loaded.

The Takahashi Rural Improvement Association

Requests the City Government to Pilot the Baojia System

Du Yuesheng Aims to Promote Local Undertakings

Orders Public Security Organs to Preside, with the Association Assisting

The Takahashi Rural Improvement Association, in view of the fact that the Baojia system is the primary plan for local autonomy, and since its implementation in various provinces and counties has achieved great success, Shanghai, although located in the economic and cultural center of the country, still lacks this organization, resulting in numerous difficulties when promoting local undertakings. Although Takahashi is located in the eastern rural area of Shanghai, after the enthusiastic efforts of local people in recent years, everything is waiting to be done. The implementation of the Baojia system is urgently needed as a basis for launching undertakings. The association has been engaged in the construction of rural Takahashi for two years, and deeply feels that the masses lack organization. Therefore, the rise and fall of an event cannot grasp the main points and achieve the effect of cooperation between the masses and the government. All organizations engaged in rural undertakings in Takahashi also feel the same pain of being uncertain and lacking a basis. Striving hard often achieves half the result with twice the effort. Therefore, we hereby state the facts and earnestly request your government to approve the pilot implementation of the Baojia system in the Takahashi District, and within a short period of time, instruct the local public security organs to preside over it. The association will also do its best to assist, so that we can see the success as soon as possible. If the public security organs are too busy with government affairs, and instruct the association to preside over it, we are also willing to devote all our efforts to serve our government and the local area. After the Xi'an Incident

Northwest Intermodal Transport Interrupted

Goods Unloaded at Lianyungang Pier

Shipments to Shanghai Stopped

Since the Xi'an Incident occurred, the traffic on the Longhai Railway was blocked, and the intermodal transport of goods from Shanghai was also affected. According to Section Chief Wang of the Intermodal Transport Section of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, due to the poor wheat harvest in the Northwest this year, a large amount of flour and rice was purchased from Shanghai. Currently, there are 14,000 to 15,000 tons being transported from Shanghai. When they arrived at Lianyungang, the Xi'an Incident broke out, and the Longhai Railway was interrupted. These grains could not be shipped to the Northwest and had to be temporarily unloaded in the Lianyungang warehouse. The warehouses are already full of goods to be shipped, and there is no way to store them. Therefore, the Intermodal Transport Section of the company, in order to take into account the losses of customers who are obstructed and delayed, has stopped shipping intermodal transport goods from Shanghai to the Northwest. It will be necessary to wait for the Longhai Railway to be fully open and the accumulated goods in the old kiln to be shipped out before continuing to transport them. As for the goods transported from the Northwest to Shanghai, they arrived in Haizhou before the Xi'an Incident and were waiting to be transported. The Hairen and Huahaiyun ships have been sent to load them.

Western Newspaper Reports Japanese Soldiers

Beat a Detective Sub-Inspector

Keming Beaten Unprovokedly on the Way

European Staff Express Indignation

The "North China Daily News" reported that on Sunday evening, Keming, a senior Chinese detective sub-inspector of the Huishan Police Department, was walking along Ward Road back to the Huishan Police Department after going to the Hongkou Police Station to work, when he was suddenly beaten unprovokedly by a team of armed soldiers of the Japanese Marine Corps. The time was 6:40 PM. Keming was walking alone in plain clothes. According to reports, the location of the beating was only a few steps away from the Hongkou Police Station. One armed soldier of the Japanese Marine Corps, wearing a steel wire vest, a helmet, and holding a rifle with a bayonet, struck Keming in the neck from behind. Keming turned around to defend himself, and another soldier confronted him with a weapon. Several soldiers rushed to help, all fully armed. The soldiers surrounded Keming and threatened him with rifles and bayonets. In the nick of time, a group of Chinese police officers walked out of the police station. Keming shouted in Chinese, and the Chinese police officers ran back to the police station to report to the European officer on duty, who dispatched Sub-Inspector Buck and a team of Chinese, European, and Indian police officers to Minhang Road to rescue Keming. Then he stepped into the Hongkou Police Station, and the Japanese soldiers retreated. Keming was hit several times in the face and made a report at the police station, stating that he had not provoked the Japanese soldiers, and they had suddenly beaten him for no reason. Keming did not want to go to the hospital to verify the injury and returned to the Huishan Police Department. It is reported that Keming was in charge of investigating the case of a sailor who was shot and killed by an unknown person near Bei'er Road on November 11th, accompanied by a Japanese hostess. The murderer has not yet been identified.

China Youth Swimming Pool

Charity Performance Competition Held Yesterday

Wonderful Program, Satisfactory Results, Women's Group Exceeded Expectations

The China Youth Sports Department, in order to raise funds for the Children's Paradise Association, held a charity swimming performance competition at the association's Sichuan Road swimming pool last night. The performers were all famous male and female swimmers in the city. After three months of warm water swimming training, their results have improved dramatically. Although yesterday's competition was a performance, everyone strived to do their best, especially the women's performances. The results were excellent. The performance began with a history of swimming evolution, explained by Mr. Peng Sanmei. Starting from the first attempts of humans to swim, relying on buoyant objects for support, gradually progressing to swimming across rivers without external assistance, the performance was divided into seven sections, detailed and unusual, attracting the attention of those who have not learned to swim, which was very powerful. The second part was modern swimming techniques, divided into four major categories and eight sub-items, all modern and cutting-edge styles. The third part was the beginner's swimming method, with Huo Zhenhong demonstrating various preliminary movements, how to make the body float, how to move forward, and how to breathe and exchange air, explained by Liang Zhaoan. Next was the 160-yard men's and women's relay, divided into two groups. Zhou Xiuzhen had the best start, leading by almost half a pool, but the third person, Lin Manling, deviated midway, allowing Lin Meizhen's group to catch up, resulting in Zhou's group failing. The next was lifesaving skills. China Youth believes that lifesaving is important and should not be undertaken rashly by everyone, so a lifesaving training class was established. The performers last night were mostly trainees, which was like a results test. Everyone had skills and was very proficient, attracting much attention. Next was the men's three-person relay, performed by famous masters, which was extraordinary. Then came water acrobatics, divided into twelve items, all very exciting and interesting, especially the slippery pole, dragon boat race, long-person swim, and apple swim, which were most captivating. The slippery pole was like crossing a single-log bridge. All the contestants took turns walking on bamboo poles. In the end, the Lin Manzhen and Meiling sisters crossed successively, while only Wang Zhongcheng among the men succeeded, and the rest fell into the water. In the long-person swim, the Lin sisters, Zhou Xiuling, and Liang Jinwen were divided into two groups, and their results were not weaker than the men's. In the water arena, Wang Zhongcheng for men and Zhou Xiuling for women were undefeated champions. The most difficult task was Zhang Rongguang's underwater swim, with one foot raised out of the water, the whole body and head submerged, and advancing on the back, which was very difficult. Huo Zhenhong's sea dog swim involved somersaulting forward in the water, imitating the sea dog's style. Zhou Ruiqin's bound hands and feet swim was also impossible for those who were not well-trained. The ninth item was the 160-yard eight-person men's and women's relay, which gave the contestants an opportunity to show their usual strength. The speed and posture were perfect. Then, the chairman of the conference, Ling Xitao, gave a report. In addition to thanking the visitors, he stated that the unfinished gymnasium of the association's Eight Immortals Bridge Youth Association is now actively planning for construction, and a more perfect swimming pool will be established to promote the popularity of swimming. The association's Sichuan Road pool will also add a women's training class soon, and registration will begin soon. After the speech, there was fancy diving, with dragons soaring and tigers leaping, which was beautiful and breathtaking. Each contestant jumped twelve kinds of postures. Finally, there was a water polo match, divided into blue and white teams. The white team was stronger. Within a minute, Zhang Rongguang scored two consecutive goals, and Huo Zhenhong added another, leading 3-0. The blue team tried their best to fight back, and Zhou Ruiqin scored a long shot. In the first half, the white team led 3-1. After the break, Guo Zhenheng of the white team and Zhou Ruiqin of the blue team each scored two goals, making the situation equal. Then Zhang Rongguang of the white team scored again, ending the game with a score of 6-3, with the white team winning. The lineups of both sides are as follows:

White Team: Yu Zi, Lin Jinjiang, Guo Zhenheng, Huo Zhenhong, Zhang Rongguang

Blue Team: Chen Bao Yi, Lu Huijie, Zhong Shoujun, Wang Zhongcheng, Zhou Ruiqin

Hubei Students Can Borrow Money to Study

The National University Hubei Student Subsidy Foundation sent letters to various universities stating that most of the Hubei students in the National University are from poor families, and it is difficult to raise tuition fees, so it is a pity that useful talents cannot study further. Therefore, in the 23rd year, the National University Hubei Student Subsidy Foundation was initiated to raise a foundation, which will be loaned to poor students in installments every year for relief. The 23rd and 24th academic years have been loaned according to the rules of the foundation, which has been very beneficial to poor Hubei students. Now, the 25th academic year has already begun. The foundation has decided to continue to provide loans according to the previous methods. The number of places is limited to 40. Students in the arts and law departments account for 30% of the total (12 places), and students in the science, engineering, medical, and agricultural departments account for 70% of the total (28 places). All the rules and regulations of the foundation have been compiled and sent to your university for public announcement. If there are Hubei students who are from poor families and meet the regulations of Article 2 of the detailed rules for the foundation's loans, please issue a copy of the loan request form to them, fill it out according to the format, and send it to Xiong Guozhao, at Jia Shanben, Wuchang Road, for the board of directors to collect and forward to the foundation for review. After the review and approval, the students who requested the loan will be notified to apply for the loan in accordance with the procedures. This matter concerns helping poor students, and it is hoped that you will kindly assist in the matter.

All the exhibits that have arrived will be properly kept, and the deadline for those that have not arrived will be February 10th.

Yarn Flower Speculation on Short Squeeze in Current Month's Yarn

The Situation in the Later Market Has Already Shown Weakness

The yarn market rose in the morning and fell in the afternoon, and the situation gradually showed a hesitant trend. It is because the end of the year is approaching, and there is a period of closing accounts. In addition, some peers, because the price has entered a high level, are not indifferent to buying. However, the Osaka Sanpin yarn still rebounded high.

The Interest of Buyers Has Been Relatively Weak

The opening of the standard yarn market in the morning was because there were only three business days left in this month, and the delivery yards in the warehouse were not prosperous. Of course, there will be continuous unloads in the future, so the short-selling retailers hedged their positions. The market situation was still tight, and the prices of each month rose by 1.8 or 9 jiao to 2 yuan. After the second round, the Changfeng bulls closed their positions, and the market became looser and fell. By the time of closing, the Osaka Sanpin yarn rose sharply by 2.8-9 jiao to 3.9 yuan. (End) Discussion on the Nomenclature of "Tropical Diseases" (Middle) Little Soldier Considering the origin of the term "tropical disease," it probably originated in England after it acquired India. After becoming a colony, the British gathered various medical and health experiences they gained while operating in the colonies. They combined diseases that were unique to India with those common to both India and England. They attributed the causes to geographical and climatic factors and named them "tropical diseases." The famous London School of Tropical Medicine, as well as research and treatment institutions in Mumbai, Kolkata, Ceylon, and other places, are all venues for the advancement of this discipline. Following this, the Hamburg School of Tropical Medicine in Germany (founded by Mr. Koch) and the Batavia Institute for Tropical Diseases in the Dutch East Indies emerged. There are also specialized medical schools in various South American countries, such as the most famous Oswaldo Institute. Italy also has similar institutions. Considering their meaning and application, they are all for the purpose of understanding that knowledge of tropical medicine is the most important pioneer tool in the process of colonial development. Because when venturing into barren lands, it is necessary to prepare for resistance against the invasion of nature. At this time, the only assistance relies solely on medical and health facilities. Therefore, European and American countries that possess vast colonies in tropical regions all use national power to establish specialized institutions for treating and researching this discipline. Although there is no necessary requirement to specialize in this discipline during university medical studies, medical students, after completing their studies, if they are interested in serving in colonial health institutions (missionaries sent or volunteering to work in the tropics are also subject to this rule), must receive knowledge and work training in short-term courses at specialized tropical disease schools. They must also pass an examination and be granted a certificate before being allowed to serve. There are also universities that incorporate tropical medicine knowledge into the later stages of medical studies, such as the University of Tübingen in Germany (for missionary purposes!). Similar facilities exist in other countries, especially England, which need not be elaborated upon. Regarding the use of this discipline's name in various countries, the British Empire naturally calls it "Tropical Diseases." The United States follows the lead of its elder brother, which is self-explanatory. A part of Germany also calls it "Tropical and Maritime Diseases." However, some people call it "Exotic Diseases." This is obviously because they feel that the term "tropical disease" cannot fully encompass the meaning, and they want to use a more cautious and ambiguous term! However, when viewed objectively, it is felt that the use of these three words by European and American countries to represent the overall sum of this discipline already has sufficient justification from a geographical standpoint (except for South American countries). From a factual standpoint, these diseases are relatively rare (also excluding South America), which does not hinder the use of this term. Moreover, the roots of history and custom have already reached a considerable depth, and there is no need for reform whatsoever. Since the situation in European and American countries, the origin of the term "tropical diseases," is as such, let us turn our attention back to the Eastern Hemisphere and see what the situation is in Asia. Among the countries in Asia, besides our magnificent Republic of China, the one worth discussing is, of course, Japan. They absorbed Western civilization earlier, and their achievements are also considerable. We know that they are the best at copying, but here they did not blindly accept and imitate! Although they also have a tropical disease hospital in Kobe and an overseas medical affairs department at Keio University, these are not national institutions. There is also no specialized term in the curriculum of imperial universities. However, if we flip through their medical textbooks, we find a difference from the textbooks we use. In their textbooks, all so-called tropical diseases related to the East are sequentially incorporated. This method of extracting the essence and discarding the dross can truly be called rationalization! Emphasizing substance over name is the secret to Japan's success in absorbing Western culture! This is a clear example! I am not singing their praises; simply speaking from the perspective of position, environmental needs, and circumstances, the situations of China and Japan are identical in every way, so it is impossible not to make a comparison. If we carefully analyze tropical diseases, their main components are still infectious diseases, and parasitic organisms (including both animal and plant kingdoms) occupy the most important part beyond the scope of bacteria. Diseases caused purely by climatic factors are relatively few. At most, they become contributing factors with slightly different clinical courses. From a clinical point of view, the main field of tropical diseases lies in internal medicine. Decisively excluding skin diseases and venereal diseases, decisively excluding surgery, and other departments. Observing the above situation and for the sake of our own factual needs, at least I personally feel that we should obtain two viewpoints. Medicinal Plants of Domestic Origin (Continued) Zhou Mengbai Asclepiadaceae I. White Swallowwort Cynanchum atratum, Bunge. (Plant) Grows naturally in the mountains and fields of warm regions, a perennial herb. The entire plant is densely covered with short hairs. Leaves are opposite, thick, short-stalked, elliptical, wavy-edged, and convex-tipped. In summer, small purplish-black flowers are attached to the axils of the branches. (Crude drug) White Swallowwort Root Radix Cynanchi atrati, is collected from its roots and dried. This product has numerous slender adventitious roots branching from the root head, reaching a length of 15-20 cm. The root head generally retains residual stems. The surface is grayish-white, the texture is firm and brittle, and the taste is bitter. (Medicinal use) Old saying: White Swallowwort is a heat-clearing and diuretic drug, used for edema. II. Caudate Swallowwort Cynanchum caudatum, Maxim (Plant) Grows naturally in mountains and fields, a perennial vine. It is stout with straight roots. Leaves are opposite, long-stalked, long heart-shaped, and sharply pointed. Axillary cymes emerge, and white small flowers with long stalks bloom in summer. The follicles are lanceolate and reach a length of 7 cm. (Crude drug) Swallowwort Root Kadix Cynanchi, is collected from its roots, which are longitudinally cut and transversely sliced, and then dried. The surface of this product is light brown, transversely cut, with lenticels connected to transverse wrinkles. The texture is dense and firm. The transverse section is white and granular. The taste is slightly bitter. (Composition) The root contains Cinancotoxin. This substance does not contain nitrogen and does not contain sucrose. (Pharmacology) When 1-3 mg of Cinancotoxin is injected subcutaneously into a frog weighing 10 cm, strong intermittent convulsions occur due to the excitation of the convulsive center. The heartbeat also becomes slow, and then ceases due to paralysis of the autonomic motor center. In warm-blooded animals, epileptiform convulsions occur, accompanied by salivation, vomiting, and swimming movements of the limbs, showing the brain-induced convulsive toxicity belonging to the Picrotoxin family. (Medicinal use) Old saying: Swallowwort root is a specialized diuretic drug. III. Japanese Metaplexis Metaplexis Japonica, Makino (Plant) Grows naturally in mountains and fields, a perennial twining herb. The entire plant is densely covered with soft hairs. Leaves are opposite, long-stalked, long heart-shaped, entire, and sharply pointed. Axillary racemose inflorescences emerge, and small light purple flowers bloom in summer. The follicles are horn-shaped and lanceolate. (Crude drug) Metaplexis Seed Fructus Metapjeisx, is collected from its fruits and dried. This product is long lanceolate, reaching a length of 10 cm. The surface is light green or light brown. When mature, it splits open from the ventral suture, exposing numerous seeds. The seeds are brownish-red, flat, and elliptical, with a white silky coma, about 2 mm long. (Medicinal use) Old saying: Metaplexis seeds and leaves are invigorating drugs. Example prescription: Metaplexis seeds 16.0, Lycium Root-bark, Schisandra, Arborvitae Seed, Zizyphus Seed, Dried Rehmannia Root, 12.0 each Grind the above herbs into powder, mix, and take a small amount three times a day.

Random Thoughts on Spring and Autumn (Infatuated Goose) Only with lofty ideals can there be a lofty life. Many defects of reality must be compensated by ideals. Many sorrows of life disappear in ideals. Many hopes of life are realized because of ideals. Ideals can enable a defeated warrior to run back onto the battlefield of life. Ideals can enable a heartbroken lover to be rebaptized in the river of love. Ideals can enable Sakyamuni to abandon his throne and go alone to the lonely mountains to practice asceticism. Ideals can enable Jesus to walk resolutely to the cross with unwavering composure. Ideals can enable Newton, Watt, Edison... to become scientists. Ideals can enable Tao Yuanming, Li Bai, Du Fu... to become poets. Ideals are the compass; when you lose your way, they point you to the light. Ideals are the beacon; in the vast sea of humanity, they illuminate your path forward. With ideals, one can ascend to heaven from hell. With ideals, one can jump into paradise from the sea of suffering. Our National Flag Yan Chonglou What we respect is our national flag. What we are responsible for is guarding our national flag on the border. The enemy wants to destroy our national flag and annex our territory. This conspiracy has been brewing for a long time, but we cannot let them do it, because the life of the national flag is our life. In the star- and moonlit night, our national flag flutters in the gale. We do not miss our parents in our hometown, nor do we yearn for a leisurely life. We lie in the trenches, holding our rifles in our hands and hand grenades on our chests. Although the fierce wind blows in our faces, this fierce wind, which would normally enter our nostrils, might stop our breathing, freeze off our fingers, and make us lie stiff and wait for death. But today, oh today, we have the courage to prepare for a decisive battle! We have a fire burning inside us! We do not flinch at all! We are not afraid of the cold at all! Each of us is a ball of flame! In the vast expanse of yellow sand, surrounded by nothingness, we have not slackened our spirits. We keep our eyes wide open. When we see the enemy approaching, we do not disturb them at first. When the enemy gets close, we fire our guns in unison. Then, some enemies fall to the ground, and some flee. Sometimes, our blood boils, and we leap out of the trenches. Regardless of how rugged the road is, we rush towards the enemy, upholding our national flag and marching forward! The national flag is our soul. We want to seek freedom and liberation for our soul. The national flag is in front of us, giving us encouragement and comfort. As long as the national flag exists, our spirit will not die. The Girl Without a Motherland Zhu Ying The rain was falling torrentially. Two rickshaws carried two lost souls of the city along a flat and dim road at night. One was me, and the other was my friend A Wei. I was specially accompanying A Wei to sightsee because he had discovered a miracle. It was said to be a noble lady from a certain European royal family who had just arrived from the United States, but she was now without a motherland. Not only was she young and beautiful, but she was also proficient in music, singing, and dancing. Therefore, as the wheels rolled along a certain road, I kept chewing on everything that A Wei had told me—according to A Wei, he had already been there three times, and this was the fourth time, because he wanted to consult her about music. Indeed, A Wei knew music. At A Wei's direction, the rickshaw puller turned a corner and finally stopped in front of a very old small Western-style house. He rang the doorbell, and a Chinese servant appeared from inside the door. When he saw A Wei, he said with a smile, "What a coincidence, Miss Tairoki just returned." A Wei nodded and led me straight to a bedroom on the third floor. Beautiful piano music drifted out melodiously. The sound of students' footsteps startled the music to a stop. A Russian girl, indeed very beautiful, came out of the room to greet A Wei and held my hand tightly, using stiff English to invite us into the room. After talking for a while, A Wei told her that he had brought a friend to appreciate her songs. As he spoke, he pointed to me. The girl smiled at me, then stood up abruptly, took out a violin from the cabinet, played it, and sang a small Parisian tune in a melodious voice. Then, she changed the tune and sang a Russian song. As she sang to the end, mournful notes jumped out with the strings, and tears couldn't help but jump out of her long eyelashes. But as soon as the song ended, she wiped away her tears and laughed again. During the conversation, I learned that she was only twenty years old this year. When she was five years old, she drifted to Paris with her parents. Then, her father died, and life became increasingly difficult. In the past ten years or so, she had experienced the hardships of the world. For the past eight years, she had been relying entirely on singing to support herself. She had wandered around New York, Chicago, and other places for three or four years, but she couldn't find a stable life. Recently, she had drifted to the Far East with her mother, like an autumn leaf. If she couldn't gain a foothold here, she might cross the sea to Japan again. The three hours quickly slipped away in wisps of cigarette smoke. I took out my watch and looked at it. The short hand was pointing to almost eleven o'clock, so I got up and pulled A Wei to leave. The girl suddenly brought her blood-red lips close to A Wei's ear, smiled charmingly, and said softly. A Wei smiled and said to me, "I'm not leaving. She said she'll find you a girlfriend to keep you company, how about that?" As he spoke, he made a face. I shook my head, put on my raincoat, and bid farewell to return to my residence. On the way back, I felt very empty in my heart, and I couldn't say exactly what kind of discomfort it was.

Knocking for Coregonus Nicholsii Luo Futing Knocking for Coregonus nicholsii, this unfamiliar method of catching fish, is something I only learned from my wife recently. It seems that the hearing of this fish favors musical sounds. Fishermen take advantage of this weakness, using knocking sounds to lure it into the net. Because the fish loves to listen to music, it mistakenly enters the net, thus losing its life. It can be seen that in this world, all things will inevitably lead to sorrow after extreme joy. But the person who discovered that this fish has an organ that likes to listen to music is no less accomplished than the Western musician Beethoven! Because there are many fishing households who rely on this method of catching fish to make a living. In the setting sun, when taking a walk on the motor road along the bank of Jiu—Xijiu in the western suburbs of Yixing—in addition to enjoying the leisurely scenery, we can sometimes hear a rhythmic, monotonous knocking sound, gently carried by the evening breeze. At first, people may wonder if it is a child on a fishing boat knocking for fun, or a signal to urge some kind of waterfowl to return, but after a few days, I saw the performance of this fact: that small fishing boat curved in from the small river mouth connecting to Xijiu, Boom—Ping Boom—Boom Ping Boom Ping Ping Boom Ping… Suddenly, the person paddling at the stern of the boat skillfully and rhythmically steps on a small movable wooden board placed on the boat surface. His technique of using both hands and feet requires considerable training. The sound of the knocking is very much like reading a seven-character quatrain poem when adjusting the tones, monotonous, weary, and sluggish. They don't ask whether it's spring, summer, autumn, or winter; whether it's sunny, rainy, snowing, or windy. They always spend their long years in this monotonous and weary life. When the wind and rain blow gray hair onto their heads, their age is soon aged by hard work, but their work is still a new beginning, as if destined in a previous life. If you hear this desolate melody on a drizzly early winter afternoon, a piercingly painful scar can immediately be imprinted on your brain—this is a miserable cry for survival!

The Patient Using an Iron Lung at Peking Union Medical College (Part 1) Bi Li Last spring, an American wealthy businessman from Chicago, Mr. Snyder, traveled to China with his family. After they arrived in Shanghai, Mr. Snyder and others boarded a ship northward, but Mr. Snyder's son and a friend took a plane to Beiping. The night before boarding the plane, he caught a cold. On the plane, he felt dizzy and unbearable. When he arrived in Beiping, his friend saw that his condition was not good, so he sent him to Peking Union Medical College Hospital. Two hours after arriving at the hospital, half of his body was stiff and unable to move. The doctor rushed to use an iron lung to maintain his breathing, otherwise, in another half an hour, his life would have been beyond saving, because his own lungs had reached a critical state of being unable to breathe. What exactly is the structure of this iron lung? It is an iron box shaped like a coffin. The patient lies inside the box, with only his head exposed. The patient's neck is surrounded by a very soft rubber ring. This iron box is connected to a specially made air pump. First, air is forced into the iron box—all the openings of the box are airtight—so the patient's lungs are also subjected to pressure and exhale; then, the air is extracted, so the patient's lungs expand due to the reduced pressure and can inhale air. The rate at which the pump presses and extracts is adjusted to be equal to the time of a normal person's inhalation and exhalation. In this way, the patient's lungs continue their breathing function under passive conditions. The side wall of the iron lung is fitted with two transparent membrane windows, and the doctor can look inside to see the internal conditions. There are also four pistons on the iron lung, and the doctor can reach in to move the position of the patient's limbs. The bedding inside the iron lung also needs to be changed; this is a very troublesome task. Twelve nurses need to work together to remove the bedding within three seconds. Because if the function of the iron lung is stopped for more than three seconds, then the patient will not be able to withstand the pain. After a quarter of an hour, the clean bedding is changed in within three seconds.

A Sojourn to Yan Hui's Former Residence Chen Jie —In the Humble Alley of Qufu— Yan Hui was the most admired of Confucius's three thousand disciples and the most virtuous of the seventy-two sages. Because he received Confucius's extreme praise, he was given the honorary title of "Assistant Sage" and was revered by later generations of scholars. Unfortunately, he did not enjoy a long life and died young in his youth. Confucius felt infinite sorrow at the death of this outstanding disciple. From the Analects, we know that Yan Hui was very poor during his lifetime. He lived in a dilapidated alley, but he did not suffer because of it and was able to maintain his joy as before. In Confucius's eyes, this attitude of being content with poverty was considered a manifestation of Yan Hui's virtue, and later generations of people who read the Analects also passed this matter down as a beautiful story. Where exactly is this humble alley? If you have the opportunity to go to Qufu, you can find its remains. Originally, on the way from the Confucius Temple to the Confucius Forest, there is a narrow street, just like the ordinary streets of Qufu. At the intersection stands a stone archway with the clear words "Humble Alley" engraved on it. On both sides of the street are scattered small, tilted houses and several bald thatched huts. It is said that this is the humble alley where Yan Hui lived in his time. Now that we see the true situation, it is indeed very dilapidated. But it is clearly a street, why is it called an alley? I think it is probably that the humble alley was the original site, which was transformed into a street after changes in later generations. There is also a temple of Yan Hui in the humble alley, with the words "Yan Temple" written on the door lintel. Although the architecture is not as grand and magnificent as the Confucius Temple, it generally has red walls and tall gate towers, which not only arouse solemn thoughts in visitors, but also serve as the only embellishment in this humble alley, adding a lot of color to it. The Yan Temple is worth describing in detail. In front of the temple gate is a very large meadow, interspersed with many ancient trees of unknown names, which grow very thick and tall. I don't know how many years they have been around. At a glance, they give people a sense of ancient times. Entering the temple gate, in that corner, you can see an ancient well, called "Humble Alley Well." The well is very deep, but the well water has long since dried up. Looking down, one only feels a dark darkness, unable to see anything. Around the well is a dilapidated thatched pavilion. If you sit idly on the railings of the thatched pavilion, overlooking this mysterious ancient well, and thinking about the scene of Yan Hui drawing water and drinking here thousands of years ago, how mysterious will you feel in your heart? In front of the pavilion, there is also a tree that is even older than the ancient trees in front of the gate. The trunk has cracked, and it may be destroyed by wind and rain at any time. Now it is tightly surrounded by iron rings, which complements the ancient well and thatched pavilion. If you go further into the hall, you will reach the main hall. Looking up, you can see Yanzi, who died young, sitting there solemnly, receiving the worship of future generations. Although he has no beard, in such a towering and grand temple, he also shows a solemn demeanor. Unfortunately, the tall temple was bombarded beyond repair by Zhang Zongchang's Zhili-Shandong army years ago. Now, part of the roof is exposed to the sky. It is pitiful that Yanzi's shrine has to be padded with a very thick and large bamboo mat, with stones pressing down on the four corners, which can barely avoid wind and rain. From this, we are sad about the inferiority of his fate, even after death he cannot peacefully enjoy a very good temple. At the same time, we deeply feel the odiousness of the warlords, who, in order to fight for power and profit, ruthlessly destroy thousands of years of historical sites. I don't know how many have been sacrificed, and it is not just the Yan Temple alone? It is said that there are currently no descendants of Yan Hui in Qufu, because there were no descendants left at that time. As for the annual sacrifices at the Yan Temple, they are presided over by local gentry, but they are only a perfunctory effort and do not have the solemn respect of the Confucius Temple's sacrificial ceremonies. This is also the bitterness of not having descendants!

Changing the Nest and Replacing the Phoenix Written by Zhang Henshui Episode 9 Pledging Hearts with a Cup of Water, Talking Wearily in the Green Light Hooking Fingers and Promising Love with Red Beans Guo Qi smiled: I'm just here to cool off. As the saying goes, a calm mind is naturally cool. I sit here without moving, so I don't need to use a fan, and it's still very cool. Old Mrs. Zhang said, "That's enough for today. Tomorrow, get up early and go for a walk. Sitting at home all day in this hot weather will make you sick." Guo Qi thought that although his mother's words came from love, he felt very depressed in his heart, so it would be good to go out for a walk. Later, after reading the two postscripts, he understood that he had left a note asking people to wait. Based on his personality, he is very enthusiastic. And since he volunteered to deliver messages between the two sides, he would be even more enthusiastic. The note says that he did not talk in detail. Probably there is something in these four words "did not talk in detail" that cannot be said face to face. In that case, just wait for him at home. Thinking this in his heart, he held the note in both hands and just stood up. It was at this time that someone asked in the courtyard: "Is Mr. Zhang back?" It was Li Youmei's voice. He nodded to Guo Qi and smiled, "Brother, you came back early. I came a while ago and talked with your mother for a long time." As he spoke, he took a seven-inch small flower fan and kept waving it in front of his chest. (113)

Shen Bao Local Supplement People Without Children Lyon It's like a dream. The era of wearing melon-skin hats with red pom-poms seems to be right before my eyes, and I'm already the father of two children. My own father is in my hometown, spending his lonely twilight years with my mother. My brother and I are blown away by the hurricane of life. It is difficult to enjoy the so-called "joy of family." Every time I receive a letter from my father, he always expresses great regret about this matter. "Others who left home with you all have children and grandchildren, laughing and talking, while our old couple sits silently in the hall, old eyes looking at old eyes, how desolate, like people without children..." These expressions of emotion often make me look at my own children, and from the bottom of my heart, seep out sad tears of sorrow. And in his most recent letter, he specifically mentioned Rong Deber in the village. He is indeed a lonely old man without children or a partner. It is said that he died in this epidemic of malignant malaria. There was no Buddhist service, no filial sons wailing, no daughters-in-law wearing hemp clothing, no one truly shedding tears. His nephews and nieces hastily collected his body and buried him that day, coldly and quietly. "Alas! Can this be considered a lifetime? This life is too in vain." My father sighed on the eight-line letter with heavy sentences. From his sighing sentences, I felt the sorrow of people without children. This sorrow, for Rong Deber himself, was naturally not after death, but before death. Quietly, from the sad emotion, Rong Deber revived in my memory: He was such a loyal and kind elder. Below his eight-character mustache was a mouth that always seemed to be smiling. His cheekbones were very high because his muscles were too thin. His dim old eyes were deeply sunken in his hollow eye sockets, caused by chronic weeping due to severe trachoma. His gray hair only circled the back of his head. His long cloth gown was shiny with oil, and the sleeves were particularly bright. The lining of his cloth shirt was never washed year-round. He spent less time at home and more time wandering the streets. He was a regular at the Dongyuan Teahouse. He didn't talk much to people. Like a hedgehog, he huddled at a table near the stove, sometimes blankly puffing on his long-stemmed pipe. Some people secretly called him "Cut-off Butt." People in the village didn't welcome him when they had happy events, as if his arrival would affect the bride's fertility. Everyone gave him unfriendly looks. Even his own brothers had grudges with him. According to his brothers' suggestion, they wanted to establish his nephew as his heir to inherit his property. Several times, but he refused each time: "Why must I have a son? I earned the property myself, I suffered myself, can't I enjoy it myself? Biological children sometimes make you angry and suffer in old age!" This was the only reason he held. Later, he even sold a few acres of farmland, ignoring the objections of his nephews, and even turned a plot of pit latrine into money. He spent the whole day wandering the streets eating mutton, drinking alcohol, and playing cards. As long as he considered someone trustworthy, he would generously lend ten or eight dollars. Even if he was cheated, he didn't care. Because of this, his relatives said to him with resentment: "Who do you want to harm when you die?" "Die? Hehehehe... The King of Hell keeps me for one more day, and I will enjoy one more day. It's still a lifetime. No children, no children... Alas, everything is empty. Death is death. Who can I harm!" His answer was always these few sentences. Was this his way of seeing through his own life? There, I remember very clearly; the year my second brother got married, he stood under the eaves of my house and said to my father these miserable words: "Old brother, you really accumulated blessings in your previous life. Two sons, the elder daughter-in-law added a grandson, and the second daughter-in-law also entered the house. A family of three generations, three generations... Look at me, older than you, all alone. If I didn't commit sins in my previous life, Heaven wouldn't punish me to this extent. Good, you old brother should understand, having a son is all you need..." And now, according to my father's letter, he is dead. I know that although he is dead, his regret of not having children has not died. The hometown is such a strange place. It will ridicule a person without children, try to seize the property of a person without children, and consider him unlucky. But, what about those who have children and descendants? Doesn't my father have two sons? But they are blown away by the hurricane of life all year round, making their parents "seem like people without children."

Factories Forced to Shut Down Due to Depletion of Raw Materials Jianping On the eleventh, I said in "Tan Yan": "The soaring prices of everything are not a good phenomenon." That was just "some unscrupulous merchants taking the opportunity to monopolize, even hoarding necessary goods and even food," causing "the number of rice ships arriving at port to decrease daily, and the rice market to see a more severe price surge." There, I only used food as an example to prove the correctness of the statement "the soaring prices of everything are not a good phenomenon." At the same time, I pointed out that the current abnormal phenomenon of "constantly rising prices" is a "man-made" conspiracy. However, such a proposition also encountered criticism from some commentators. However, the facts are the most eloquent. Now let me say another paragraph, which is also caused by the "hoarding and speculation" of some unscrupulous merchants, which has led to even more tragic facts, to prove that this is indeed a "man-made" conspiracy. On the twelfth, this newspaper's local news had the following item: "After the decline in the price of Chinese silk in the European and American markets, 40 silk factories in Shanghai have all stopped work one after another due to the depletion of raw materials. As of yesterday (the eleventh), more than ten factories including Hengtai and Zhenxiang have stopped work; Dongxiang, Yufeng, etc. have also run out of raw materials and will stop work immediately; as for the remaining factories that are still operating, such as Jiyu, it is expected that all will stop by the end of January." We have seen news of yarn factories being "forced to shut down" due to "depletion of raw materials," but it is unprecedented to hear that all are "willing to shut down and unwilling to continue driving." Since the yarn factories are "forced to shut down" because of "depletion of raw materials," then why are the raw materials depleted? The undoubtedly answer is that this is another trick of unscrupulous merchants. In the same issue of the news, we see that the cause of this "depletion of raw materials" is partly due to "the poor harvest of autumn cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang this year, which is not enough for silk factories to use," but the main reason is still "although general cocoon merchants have purchased a large amount of this year's bumper spring cocoons, they are hoarding and speculating because they are aware that the European and American silk markets have improved somewhat between September and October, and are unwilling to sell lightly." So, from this, we can know that the reason for this "forced shutdown of yarn factories" is somewhat problematic to say that it is due to "depletion of raw materials." To put it more clearly: the raw materials are there, but the general unscrupulous merchants hope to "hoard and speculate," and will not let go until they have made a big fortune, so they are "unwilling to sell lightly." Then how can it be "depletion of raw materials"? Of course, we cannot blame the general manufacturers too much. Businessmen have their own business scriptures, and no one is willing to do a loss-making business. Don't we see: "According to a survey by the silk industry, there are still 10,000 to 20,000 dan of cocoons stored in Shanghai foreign firms. If manufacturers purchase them, they cannot make a profit at the current silk market due to the high price." Then how can we blame them for being "willing to shut down and unwilling to continue driving"? The raw materials have already been exploited by the "hoarders" for the first time, and the cost has increased, making it unaffordable for general small industrialists; however, the sales of finished products and the silk market are also "seeing a decline in overseas markets due to the speculative activities of speculators." Repeatedly giving the intermediate merchants (of course, we cannot ignore their backstage bosses) direct and indirect exploitation, how can they not "fall without being hit"? The terrible fact that Tianjin's privately owned yarn factories have been swallowed one after another is a lesson from the past. Whether for the sake of the country or for the sake of the national industry, how can we lightly regard and ignore this tragic event. Others rely on their special political power as a cover, and under the beautiful name of "economic cooperation," they carry out all plans to destroy us "without seeing blood." What about us? The weak national industry has no strong support, which goes without saying, and the general unscrupulous merchants who only see "self-interest" dare to illegally slaughter their own national industry, regardless of whether there is a background or not, we always believe that it is a "hating my pain" disaster for the country. To those who are engaged in our "inherently insufficient" pitiful national industry, we dare to earnestly advise: we have no other way to make the national industry develop freely under protection except to consolidate our national defense.

The Special Maritime Party Department of China convened various maritime organizations at 10:00 AM yesterday for a memorial week to condemn traitors. The meeting adjourned around 11:00 AM. Details follow:

Chairman's Report

After Chairman Yang Hu led the attendees in customary salutations, he delivered a report, stating in brief: "Zhang Xueliang, entrusted with significant military responsibilities and the recipient of Chairman Chiang's unparalleled benevolence, has failed to reciprocate with gratitude. Instead, he has dared to rebel, seizing the commander-in-chief. Our government, responding to the people's demands, is righteously and justly condemning him. All Chinese seamen should strive to be the government's support, aiming to swiftly quell the rebellious atmosphere and ensure the early and safe return of our esteemed leader to the capital, to lead the entire nation in completing the great revolutionary cause."

Pledge

Following the chairman's report, all participants took an oath, the text of which read: "I pledge with utmost sincerity to be loyal to the Party and the Nation, to support Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. If I betray this oath, I am willing to accept the most severe punishment from this Party."

(7) In order to revive the nation, we should oppose all reactionary parties that disperse the central government's strength and deprive the motherland's interests. We advocate national unity, support the Three Principles of the People, and melt the thoughts of the Chinese people into one furnace, in order to unify actions, align steps, and create a kind of great invincible force. (8) We look forward to the early release of the revolutionary leader from danger, and we hope that Zhang Xueliang and his subordinates, as well as those suffering from the same disease as Zhang, will immediately repent of their past mistakes and unanimously work hard to resist foreign aggression under the command of the central government. At the same time, we hope that everyone will loudly shout, 'Return our revolutionary leader Chiang Kai-shek to freedom!' Use the power of the true 'People's Front' to rescue the leader back to the capital, preside over the major plans of the country, eliminate the remaining warlords, eradicate the Red bandits who harm the country, eliminate all reactionary parties, concentrate forces, consolidate the central government, and support the National Government. Long live the Three Principles of the People, long live Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, long live the Republic of China."

First Flying Academy Training Class Graduation Exam; 21 Tested Yesterday, Continuing Today; Results Announced and Certificates Issued on a Set Date 85

The first flying training class established by the China Flying Academy, which began in mid-June of this year, has now completed its originally scheduled curriculum and is capable of flying solo. Graduation exams began yesterday morning. The academy received approval from the Central Aviation Commission to send Yao Xijiu to supervise the exams. Approximately 30 students who have completed the curriculum are being tested one by one. Testing will be completed tomorrow, and results will be announced on a set date. The Aviation Construction Commission and the government will be requested to award certificates, and a graduation ceremony will be held on a set date to issue certificates. The details of the examination are recorded below:

Students Taking the Exam: Zheng Liren, Lu Jiying, Zai Pengcheng, Peng Han, Zhou Picheng, Luo Qianzhong, Zhu Tiefu, Wu Zhaokun, He Youliang, Chen Xiangyin, Li Keqing, Huang Jingkui, Wang Boshu, Shen Yubing, Yao Peng, Pan Xi, Gu Yaxiong, Shen Anlin, Wang Dixing, Yang Jinxun, and Sui Shixin, an employee from the mechanical section. Wang Guanyu, Li Lian, Zheng Xiaolun, Cui Xiangming, Cai Jinlong, Zhang Ying, Zhou Jingyao, Bai Shizhong, Wen Zhenxin, Sun Wenming, Chen Jiachen, and mechanic Song Mingxiang will continue the exam today.

Exam Subjects: (1) Takeoff, (2) Navigation Route, (3) Landing, (4) Straight and Level Flight, (5) Large Turns, (6) Medium Turns, (7) Small Turns, (8) Wingovers, (9) Spiral Descent, (10) Figure-8 Turns, (11) Forced Landing.

Exam Supervisors: Yao Xijiu, Counselor appointed by the Central Aviation Commission, and Wu Tiecheng, President of the academy, Wang Xiaolai, Vice President. Exam officials: Chen Buzhou, Director of the Academy's Flight Section, Yang Guozhu, Director of the Research Section and Flying Instructor, and instructors Chen Shenhu and Yang Zhaofan.
